تجوز به قادح في أصل الشريعة ، ولا معطل ونسبوا كل من ينزه البارى تعالى وجل عن النقائص والآفات وينفى عنه الحدوث والتشبيهات ويقدسه عن الحلول والزوال ويعظمه عن التغير من حال إلى حال ، وعن حلوله في الحوادث وحدوث الحوادث فيه إلى الكفر والطغيان ، ومنافاة أهل الحق والإيمان وتناهوا في قذف الأئمة الماضين وثلب أهل الحق وعصابة الدين ، ولعنهم في الجوامع والمشاهد والمحافل والمساجد والأسواق والطرقات والخلوة والجماعات ، ثم غرهم الطمع والأهمال ومدهم في طغيانهم الغى والضلال إلى الطعن فيمن يعتضد به أئمة الهدى وهو للشريعة العروة الوثقى وجعلوا أفعاله الدينية معاصى دنية ، وترقوا من ذلك إلى القدح في الشافعي رحمة الله عليه وأصحابه واتفق عود الشيخ الإمام الأوحد أبى نصر ابن الأستاذ الإمام زين الإسلام أبى القسم القشيري رحمة الله عليه ، من مكة حرسها الله فدعا الناس إلى التوحيد وقدس البارى عن الحوادث والتحديد فاستجاب له أهل التحقيق من الصدور الأفاضل السادة الأماثل وتمادت الحشوية في ضلالتها والاصرار على جهالتها وأبوا إلا التصريح بأن المعبود ذو قدم وأضراس ولهوات وأنامل وأنه ينزل بذاته ويتردد على حمار فى صورة شاب أمرد بشعر قطط ، وعليه تاج يلمع وفى رجليه نعلان من ذهب وحفظ ذلك عنهم وعللوه ودونوه في كتبهم وإلى العوام القوه ، وأن هذه الأخبار لا تأويل لها وأنها تجري على ظواهرها وتعتقد كما ورد لفظها وأنه تعالى يتكلم بصوت كالرعد وكصهيل الخيل
He permits criticism that harms the foundation of the Sharia, and there is no one who negates [attributes], and they attribute everyone who declares the Creator, exalted and majestic, free from deficiencies and defects, negates from Him temporal origination and anthropomorphisms, sanctifies Him from incarnation and cessation, magnifies Him from change from state to state, and from His incarnation in originated things and the origination of originated things in Him—they attribute [such a person] to unbelief and transgression, and opposition to the people of truth and faith. They went to extremes in slandering the past imams, reviling the people of truth and the party of religion, and cursing them in congregational mosques, shrines, assemblies, masjids, markets, roads, in private and in congregations. Then greed and negligence deceived them, and error and misguidance extended them in their transgression to attacking the one whom the imams of guidance rely upon, who is the firmest handhold of the Sharia, and they considered his religious actions as base sins. They escalated from that to attacking al-Shafi'i, may God have mercy on him and his companions. It coincided with the return of the unique teacher Abu Nasr, son of the teacher Imam Zayn al-Islam Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri (may God have mercy on him) from Mecca, may God protect it. He called the people to tawheed and declared the Creator transcendent over temporal events and limitation, so the people of verification from the foremost nobles and virtuous leaders responded to him. But the Hashwiyya persisted in their misguidance and insistence on their ignorance, and they refused except to declare that the worshipped being has foot, molars, uvula, fingers, and that He descends in His essence and moves about on a donkey in the form of a beardless youth with curly hair, wearing a shining crown and on his feet two sandals of gold. They preserved that [statement] from them, explained it, and recorded it in their books, and they threw it to the common people. And [they said] that these reports have no interpretation, that they are taken literally and believed as their wording came, and that He, exalted, speaks with a voice like thunder and like the neighing of horses.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is an indictment of the Hashwiyya sect. It begins by accusing them of slandering those who uphold tanzih (transcendence) and attribute to them disbelief. Then it lists their anthropomorphic claims: that God has body parts (foot, molars, etc.), descends, rides a donkey, etc. It also mentions that they reject ta'wil (interpretation) of scriptural passages and take them literally. The passage serves to document the extreme anthropomorphism that the Ash'aris opposed.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Hashwiyya were a marginal group with no influence, but this passage shows they were powerful enough to publicly curse and slander scholars.
Correction: The passage indicates the Hashwiyya were organized and aggressive, using public venues to attack their opponents.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which Imam did the Hashwiyya escalate to attacking?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Malik ibn Anas
C) Al-Shafi'i
D) Ahmad ibn Hanbal

Key Takeaway
The Hashwiyya not only held anthropomorphic beliefs but also actively persecuted the Ash'ari scholars who defended tanzih, while al-Qushayri led a response calling people to true tawheed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Have you ever avoided declaring God's complete transcendence because it might bring criticism from others? How does your fear of people compare to your love for God's tanzih?
?
The Hashwiyya considered religious actions of true scholars as base sins. Whose opinion about your practice of Islam do you fear most—the righteous scholars or the ignorant masses?

Appeal to the Ruler: Ibn Asakir's Call for Support Against the Hashwiyya
Ibn Asakir appeals to the ruler to support the Ash'ari cause and discipline the Hashwiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir uses rhetoric and religious authority to appeal to the ruler to suppress the anthropomorphist Hashwiyya faction, and the responsibilities he places on the ruler.

Core Idea
Ibn Asakir holds the ruler accountable for defending true doctrine.

In this passage, Ibn Asakir makes a passionate plea to the ruling authority to intervene against the Hashwiyya, whom he considers misguided anthropomorphists. He combines flattery of the ruler's power with a stark warning of religious decline and personal accountability on the Day of Judgment. This lesson unpacks his rhetorical strategy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the tone—it is both reverent and urgent.
2
Identify the three threats
Ibn Asakir warns of three consequences if the ruler does not act: loss of support for truth, return of Islam to strangeness, and divine accountability on the Day of Judgment. Find where he states each.
3
Analyse the flattery and authority
Observe how Ibn Asakir elevates the ruler with honorific titles and reminds him of his vast power and divine appointment. How does this strengthen the appeal?
4
Reflect on historical context
Consider why Ibn Asakir wrote this appeal. It is a specific plea for the Ash'ari community, not a general political theory. How does knowing this shape your understanding?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما لهذه العصابة مستند ولا للحق مغيث يعتمد إلا الله تعالى ورأفة المجلس السامي الأجلى العالمى العادلى القوامي النظامى الرضوى ، أمتعه الله بحياة يأمن خطوبها باسمة فلا يعرف قطوبها فإن لم ينصر ما أظهره ويشيد ما أسسه وعمره بأمر جزم وعزم حتم يزجر أهل الغواية عن غيهم ، ويردع ذوى العناد عن بغيهم ويأمر بالمبالغة في تأديبهم ، رجع الدين بعد تبسمه قطوبا وعاد الإسلام كما بدأ غريبا وعيونهم ممتدة إلى الجواب بنيل المأمول والمزاد ، وقلوبهم متشوفة إلى النصرة والامداد فإن هو لم ينعم النظر في الحادث الذي طرقهم ويصرف معظم هممه العالية إلى الكارث الذي أزعجهم وأقلقهم ويكشف عن الشريعة هذه الغمة ويخسم نزعات الشيطان بين هذه الأمة كان عن هذه الظلامة يوم القيامة مسؤولا إذ قد أديت إليه النصائح والامانات من أهل المعارف والديانات وبرئوا من عهدة ما سمعوه بما أدوه إلى سمعه العالي وبلغوه والحجة الله تعالى متوجهة نحوه بما مكنه في شرق الأرض وغربها وبسط قدرته في عجمها وعربها وجعل إليه القبض والابرام واصطفاه من جميع الانام فما ترد نواهيه وأوامره ولا تعصى مراسمه وزواجره والله تعالى بكرمه يوفقه ويسدده ويؤيد مقاصده ويرشده ويقف فكرته وخواطره على نصرة ملته وتقوية دينه وشريعته بمنه ورأفته وفضله ورحمته
And this faction has no support, nor does the truth have a helper to rely on except God Almighty and the compassion of the lofty, most illustrious, learned, just, al-Qawwami, al-Nizami, al-Radawi council—may God grant him a life whose calamities are safe and smiling so that he knows no frowns. For if he does not support what he has manifested and strengthen what he has founded and built with a decisive command and a determined resolve that rebukes the people of misguidance from their error, deters the stubborn from their transgression, and orders intensification in disciplining them, then religion after its smile becomes frowning, and Islam returns as it began—strange. Their eyes are extended to the answer by achieving the hope and increased desire, and their hearts are yearning for victory and support. If he does not kindly consider the incident that has befallen them and direct his lofty concerns to the calamity that has disturbed and unsettled them, and uncover from the Sharia this distress, and extinguish the whisperings of Satan among this nation, he will be held responsible for this oppression on the Day of Judgment, since sincere advice and trusts have been conveyed to him from the people of knowledge and religions, and they are absolved of the responsibility of what they heard by conveying it to his lofty ear and informing him. And the argument of God Almighty is directed towards him because He has empowered him in the east of the earth and its west, extended his power over its non-Arabs and Arabs, placed in his hand contraction and ratification, and chosen him from all creatures. So his prohibitions and commands are not rejected, and his ordinances and interdictions are not disobeyed. And God Almighty, by His generosity, will grant him success, guide him, support his objectives, direct him, and fix his thought and reflections on supporting his nation and strengthening his religion and law, by His favor, grace, and mercy.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a direct appeal to the ruler (likely the sultan) to intervene on behalf of the Ash'ari community against the Hashwiyya. It uses flattery and warning: the ruler is the only hope, and if he does not act, religion will suffer and he will be accountable. It emphasizes the ruler's power and the duty to use it to suppress innovation.

Testimonies of Scholars Defending Abu Nasr al-Qushayri
Multiple scholars testify to al-Qushayri's orthodoxy and demand action against his slanderers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how three prominent scholars formally testified to the orthodoxy of Abu Nasr al-Qushayri and demanded that the ruler take action against his slanderers.

Core Idea
These testimonies are formal legal attestations confirming al-Qushayri's creed and obligating the ruler to defend him.

These three testimonies, recorded in an official record (mahdar), were written by respected scholars to defend Abu Nasr al-Qushayri against slander from anthropomorphists and other innovators. They not only confirm his unwavering adherence to Sunni creed but also stress the ruler's duty to suppress those who insult him and Imam al-Shafi'i. Reading these testimonies gives insight into the historical context of theological conflicts and the role of the state in protecting orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read the first testimony
Read the testimony of Ibrahim al-Firuzabadi. Notice how he describes al-Qushayri's activities (holding assemblies, teaching tawhid, negating tashbih) and the reaction of the innovators (envy, slander). He calls for the ruler to act.
This testimony mentions the school (madrasa) built to support the Shafi'i madhhab.
2
Compare the second testimony
Read al-Husayn al-Tabari's testimony. What additional details does he provide? He mentions that even Jews and Christians were guided by al-Qushayri, and that the slander appeared in Baghdad.
He emphasizes the ruler's responsibility and warns of sin if action is delayed.
3
Observe the third testimony
Read the third testimony (likely by Abdullah al-Karkhi). It specifies the Nizamiyya school and the use of clear evidences. Many abandoned tajsim and tashbih because of al-Qushayri's proofs.
The root cause of the slander is identified as 'extreme rage' (farṭ ghayẓihim).
4
Identify the common demand
All three testimonies call on the ruler to punish the slanderers. Why is this considered a religious obligation? Because Allah empowered the ruler, and he will be asked about it on the Day of Judgment.
This reflects the legal principle that enabling evil without intervention is sinful.
5
Reflect on the legal nature
These are not just personal praises; they are formal shahadat (attestations) that carry weight in Islamic law. How does that affect their credibility? They are binding evidence in court and impose a duty on the ruler.
The term 'shahada' implies a legal testimony with consequences.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يأمن - خطوبها باسمة فلا يعرف قطوبها فإن لم ينصر ما أظهره ويشيد ما أسسه وعمره بأمر جزم وعزم حتم يزجر أهل الغواية عن غيهم، ويردع ذوي العناد عن بغيهم ويأمر بالمبالغة في تأديبهم، رجع الدين بعد تبسمه قطوبا وعاد الإسلام كما بدأ غريبا وعيونهم ممتدة إلى الجواب بنيل المأمول والمزاد، وقلوبهم متشوفة إلى النصرة والامداد فإن هو لم ينعم النظر في الحادث الذي طرقهم ويصرف معظم هممه العالية إلى الكارث الذي أزعجهم وأقلقهم ويكشف عن الشريعة هذه الغمة ويخسم نزعات الشيطان بين هذه الأمة كان عن هذه الظلامة يوم القيامة مسؤولا إذ قد أديت إليه النصائح والامانات من أهل المعارف والديانات وبرئوا من عهدة ما سمعوه بما أدوه إلى سمعه العالي وبلغوه والحجة الله تعالى متوجهة نحوه بما مكنه في شرق الأرض وغربها وبسط قدرته في عجمها وعربها وجعل إليه القبض والابرام واصطفاه من جميع الانام فما ترد نواهيه وأوامره ولا تعصى مراسمه وزواجره والله تعالى بكرمه يوفقه ويسدده ويؤيد مقاصده ويرشده ويقف فكرته وخواطره على نصرة ملته وتقوية دينه وشريعته بمنه ورأفته وفضله ورحمته.

صورة الخطوط الأمر على ما ذكر في هذا المحضر من حال الشيخ الإمام الأوحد أبي نصر عبد الرحيم بن عبد الكريم القشيري، أكثر الله في أئمة الدين مثله من عقد المجالس وذكر الله عز وجل بما يليق به من توحيده وصفاته ونفى التشبيه عنه، وقمع المبتدعة من المجسمة والقدرية وغيرهم، ولم أسمع منه غير مذهب أهل الحق من أهل السنة والجماعة، وبه أدين الله عز وجل وإياه أعتقد وهو الذي أدركت أئمة أصحابنا عليه واهتدى به خلق كثير من المجسمة، وصاروا كلهم على مذهب أهل الحق ولم يبق من المبتدعة إلا نفر يسير فحملهم الحسد والغيظ على سبه وسب الشافعي وأئمة أصحابه. ونصار مذهبه، وهذا أمر لا يجوز الصبر عليه، ويتعين على المولى أعز الله نصره التنكيل بهذا النفر اليسير الذين تولوا كبر هذا الأمر وطعنوا في الشافعي وأصحابه، لأن الله عز وجل أقدره وهو الذي برأ في هذا البلد باعزاز هذا المذهب بما بنى فيه من المدرسة التي مات كل مبتدع من المجسمة والقدرية غيظاً منها، وبما يرتفع فيها من الأصوات بالدعاء لا يامه استجاب الله فيه صالح الأدعية، ومتى أهمل نصرهم لم يكن له عذر عند الله عز وجل. وكتب إبراهيم بن على الفيروزآبادي:

الأمر على ما ذكر في هذا المحضر من حال الشيخ الإمام الأوحد أبي نصر عبد الرحيم بن عبد الكريم القشيري جمل الله الإسلام به، وكثر في أئمة الدين مثله من عقد المجالس وذكر الله عز وجل بما وصف به نفسه من التنزيه ونفى التشبيه عنه وقمع المبتدعة من المجسمة والقدرية وغيرهم، ولم نسمع منه غير مذهب أهل الحق من أهل السنة والجماعة وبه ندين الله عز وجل وهو الذي كان عليه أئمة أصحابنا واهتدى به خلق كثير من المجسمة واليهود والنصارى فصاروا أكثرهم على مذهب أهل الحق ولم يبق من المبتدعة إلا نفر يسير فحملهم الحسد والغيظ على سبه وسب الشافعي رضي الله عنه ونصار مذهبه حتى ظهر ذلك بمدينة السلام وهذا أمر لا يحل الصبر عليه، ويتعين على من بيده قوام الدين والنظر في أمور المسلمين أن ينظر في هذا ويزيل هذا المنكر، فإن من يقدر على إزالته ويتوقف فيه يأثم ولا نعلم اليوم من جعل الله سبحانه أمر عباده إليه إلا المولى أعز الله أنصاره فيتعين عليه الإنكار على هذه الطائفة والتنكيل بهم لأن الله سبحانه أقدره على ذلك وهو المسؤول عنه غدا إن توقف فيه وصار قصد المبتدعة أكثره معاداة الفقهاء الذين هم سكان المدرسة الميمونة، فإنهم يموتون غيظاً منهم لما هم عليه من مذاكرة علم الشافعي وإحياء مذهبه. وكتب الحسين بن محمد الطبري:

الأمر على ما ذكر في هذا المحضر من حال الشيخ الإمام الأوحد أبي نصر عبد الرحيم بن عبد الكريم القشيري أدام الله حراسته، من عقد المجالس للوعظ والتذكير في المدرسة النظامية المعمورة والرباط وأطب في توحيد الله عز وجل والثناء عليه بما يستوجبه من صفات الكمال وتنزيهه عن النقائص ونفى التشبيه عنه واستوفى في الاعتقاد ما هو معتقد أهل السنة، بأوضح الحجج وأقوى البراهين فوقع في النفوس كلامه، ومال إليه الخلق الكثير من العامة ورجع جماعة كثيرة عن اعتقاد التجسيم والتشبيه، واعترفت بأنها الآن بان لها الحق فحسده المبتدعة المجسمة وغيرهم فحملهم ذلك على بسط اللسان فيه غيظاً منه، وسب الشافعي رحمة الله عليه وأئمة أصحابه ومن ينصرهم، وتظاهروا من ذلك بما لا يمكن الصبر معه ويتعين على من جعل الله إليه أمر الرعية أن يتقدم في ذلك بما يحسم مادة الفساد لأن سبب ذلك فرط غيظهم
He is safe - its calamities are smiling, so one does not know its frowns. For if he does not support what he has manifested and strengthen what he has established and built with a decisive command and firm resolve that rebukes the people of misguidance from their error, and deters the stubborn from their transgression, and orders diligence in disciplining them, then religion after its smile will frown, and Islam will return as it began, a stranger, and their eyes will be stretched toward the answer in attaining the hoped and desired, and their hearts yearning for victory and support. If he does not carefully consider the incident that has struck them and direct most of his high concerns to the calamity that has disturbed and disquieted them, and uncover this affliction from the Sharia, and sever the whisperings of Satan among this nation, he will be held responsible for this injustice on the Day of Resurrection, since sincere advice and trusts from people of knowledge and religions have been conveyed to him, and they are acquitted of the responsibility of what they heard by having conveyed it to his high hearing and communicated it. And the proof of Allah Almighty is directed toward him by what He has empowered him in the East and West of the earth, and spread his authority among its non-Arabs and Arabs, and given to him the power of binding and loosening, and chosen him from among all people. So his prohibitions and commands are not to be rejected, nor his ordinances and prohibitions disobeyed. And Allah Almighty, by His generosity, grant him success, guide him, support his goals, and direct his thought and reflections to the support of His religion and the strengthening of His faith and Sharia, by His grace, kindness, favor, and mercy.

The copy of the lines: The matter is as mentioned in this record regarding the state of the unique imam, Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn Abd al-Karim al-Qushayri — may Allah increase among the imams of religion the likes of him — of holding assemblies, mentioning Allah Almighty in a manner befitting Him of His tawhid and attributes, and negating tashbih (anthropomorphism) from Him, and suppressing the innovators from the Mujassimah (anthropomorphists) and Qadariyyah and others. And I have not heard from him except the madhhab of Ahl al-Haqq (people of truth) from Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, and by that I practice my religion to Allah Almighty, and that is my belief. And that is what I found the imams of our companions upon, and many of the Mujassimah were guided by him, and they all became upon the madhhab of Ahl al-Haqq. And only a few innovators remained, and envy and rage drove them to insult him and insult al-Shafi'i and the imams of his companions, and the supporters of his madhhab. This is a matter that cannot be tolerated, and it is incumbent upon the Mawla (ruler) — may Allah strengthen his victory — to punish this small group who have undertaken the gravity of this matter and slandered al-Shafi'i and his companions, because Allah Almighty has empowered him, and He is the one who raised him in this land to honor this madhhab by what He built therein of the school (madrasa) from which every innovator of the Mujassimah and Qadariyyah died in rage, and by what rises therein of voices in supplication, for which Allah may answer good prayers. And if he neglects their support, he will have no excuse before Allah Almighty. Written by Ibrahim ibn Ali al-Firuzabadi.

The matter is as mentioned in this record regarding the state of the unique imam Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn Abd al-Karim al-Qushayri — may Allah beautify Islam through him, and increase among the imams of religion the likes of him — of holding assemblies, mentioning Allah Almighty by what He described Himself of tanzih (transcendence) and negating tashbih from Him, and suppressing the innovators from the Mujassimah and Qadariyyah and others. And we have not heard from him except the madhhab of Ahl al-Haqq from Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, and by that we practice our religion to Allah Almighty. And that is what the imams of our companions were upon, and many of the Mujassimah, Jews, and Christians were guided by him, so most of them became upon the madhhab of Ahl al-Haqq. And only a few innovators remained, and envy and rage drove them to insult him and insult al-Shafi'i — may Allah be pleased with him — and the supporters of his madhhab, until that became apparent in the City of Peace (Baghdad). This is a matter that is not permissible to tolerate, and it is incumbent upon the one in whose hand is the pillar of religion and the authority over the affairs of Muslims to look into this and remove this evil. For whoever is able to remove it and delays in doing so sins. And today we do not know anyone to whom Allah Almighty has entrusted the affairs of His servants except the Mawla — may Allah strengthen his supporters — so it is incumbent upon him to denounce this group and punish them, because Allah Almighty has empowered him for that, and he will be asked about it tomorrow (on the Day of Judgment) if he delays. And the aim of the innovators has mostly become enmity towards the jurists who are the residents of the blessed school (madrasa), for they die of rage because of them due to their discussing the knowledge of al-Shafi'i and reviving his madhhab. Written by al-Husayn ibn Muhammad al-Tabari.

The matter is as mentioned in this record regarding the state of the unique imam Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn Abd al-Karim al-Qushayri — may Allah preserve him — of holding assemblies for preaching and reminder in the prosperous Nizamiyya school and the ribat, and persisting in the tawhid of Allah Almighty and praising Him by what He deserves of attributes of perfection and tanzih from deficiencies, and negating tashbih from Him, and he fully expounded in creed what is the creed of Ahl al-Sunna, with the clearest evidences and strongest proofs, so his speech lodged in souls. And many common people inclined to him, and a large group abandoned the belief in tajsim (anthropomorphism) and tashbih, and they acknowledged that now the truth has become clear to them. So the innovators, the Mujassimah and others, envied him, and that drove them to spread their tongues against him out of rage, and to insult al-Shafi'i — may Allah have mercy on him — and the imams of his companions and those who support them. And they have made a display of that in a way that cannot be tolerated. And it is incumbent upon the one to whom Allah has entrusted the command of the subjects to proceed in that matter in a way that cuts off the root of corruption, because the cause of that is their extreme rage.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a collection of three testimonies (shahadat) recorded in a legal document (mahdar) by three reputable scholars: Ibrahim bin Ali al-Firuzabadi, al-Husayn bin Muhammad al-Tabari, and Abdullah bin Salamah al-Karkhi. They all confirm the same facts about Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim al-Qushayri: he held assemblies to teach tawhid, negate tashbih (anthropomorphism) from Allah, and refute the innovators (Mujassimah and Qadariyyah). He only followed the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a. Many from the Mujassimah and even Jews and Christians were guided by him and abandoned their false beliefs. Only a few innovators remained, and out of envy and rage, they began to slander him and Imam al-Shafi'i. The testimonies stress that this slander cannot be tolerated and that the ruler (Mawla) must punish these slanderers, because Allah has empowered him and he will be held accountable on the Day of Judgment if he neglects this duty. The first testimony mentions the school (madrasa) built by the ruler for the support of the Shafi'i madhhab, which caused the innovators to die of rage. The second testimony adds that the slander appeared in Baghdad (Madinat al-Salam) and that the ruler must act. The third testimony specifies that al-Qushayri's sessions were in the Nizamiyya school and the ribat, and that his clear proofs led many to abandon tajsim and tashbih. All three testimonies conclude with the call for the ruler to suppress the slanderers to cut off the root of corruption.

Key Terms
المجسمة (Mujassimah)
القدرية (Qadariyyah)
التشبيه (tashbih)
التنزيه (tanzih)
أهل السنة والجماعة (Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a)
أهل الحق (Ahl al-Haqq)
المدرسة النظامية (Nizamiyya school)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These testimonies are just personal praise of al-Qushayri without legal weight.
Correction: They are formal shahadat (legal attestations) by reputable scholars, which in Islamic law carry evidentiary weight and impose obligations on the ruler to act against the slanderers.

Checkpoint
According to the testimonies, what was the main action taken by the slanderers against al-Qushayri and al-Shafi'i?
A) They openly declared disbelief in al-Qushayri's teachings.
B) They insulted (sabb) al-Qushayri and al-Shafi'i and spread slander.
C) They wrote books refuting al-Qushayri's views.
D) They established a rival school.

Key Takeaway
These three testimonies collectively establish al-Qushayri's Sunni orthodoxy and demonstrate the duty of the ruler to defend scholars from slander.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a scholar or teacher being slandered unjustly, does your heart burn with the same urgency as these scholars? What would you actually do to defend the truth? Can you think of a time you stayed silent when you should have spoken?
?
The testimonies warn that the ruler will be held accountable for neglecting this evil. You may not be a ruler, but you have influence—over your family, friends, or community. Where have you failed to act against slander or false accusations about sincere people of knowledge? How will you change that today?

Denunciation of the Hashwiyya and Appeal to the Ruler
Ibn Asakir condemns anthropomorphists and appeals to the ruler for support.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Asakir's rhetorical condemnation of nominal Muslims and his appeal for political support to defend orthodox theology.

Core Idea
True Islam is defended by righteous rulers against those who bear the name but not the substance.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari reveals the political and theological tensions of his time. He sharply denounces the Hashwiyya and mujassima as nominal Muslims whose ignorance has spread publicly. Then he turns to the ruler—likely Nizam al-Mulk—urging him to take decisive action. This lesson will unpack the rhetorical strategies and historical context.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Get a feel for the author's condemnatory tone and the shift to praise of the ruler.
Notice the contrast between the harsh opening and the flattering address to the ruler.
2
Identify the two groups condemned
Identify the terms 'mujassima' (anthropomorphists) and 'Hashwiyya' (ignorant traditionalists). What is the author accusing them of?
They are accused of being Muslims in name only and scholars by title only.
3
Understand the appeal to the ruler
How does Ibn Asakir describe the ruler? What does he demand from him? Why is the ruler's role crucial in defending the faith?
The ruler is described with widespread justice and authority; he must support the righteous and suppress the enemies.
4
Reflect on the 'first shock'
The text mentions 'الصبر في الصدمة الأولى' and a shock that distressed the Shafi'is. What might this refer to historically?
It likely refers to the initial crisis caused by the Hashwiyya, now resolved with the ruler's intervention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذمة من ناشية أغبياء المجسمة وطائفة من أرذال الحشوية استغنوا من الإسلام بالأسم ومن العلم بالرسم ، وتبعهم سوقة لانسب لهم ولا حسب ، وتظاهرت هذه اللعنة منهم في الأسواق ولم يستحسن أحد من أصحابه كثرهم الله دفع السفاهة بالسفاهة والسيئة بالسيئة ، ويجب على الناظر في أمور المسلمين من الذى قد انتشر فى المشارق والمغارب علمه وعدله ، وأمره ونهيه الذي لطاعته نبأت صدور الأولياء والأعداء ، رغبة ورهبة نصرته ومد ضبعيه والشد على يديه ، وتقديم كلمته العليا وتدحيض كلمة أعدائه السفلى فالصبر في الصدمة الأولى وهذه الصدمة التي كانت قلوب أصحاب الشافعى كثرهم الله وغرة وغلة شغله بها منذ سنين فانقشع ذلك وانكشف في هذه الأيام المؤيدة المنصورة المؤبدة النظامية القوامية العالمية العادلية نصرها الله وأعلاها وقد وقف تمامه على الأمر الماضى المنصور منه فإن في شعبة من شعب عنايته ونصرته وكلمته للدين الذى مد أطراره كفاية وبلاغا ، وعلى الغارس تعهد غراسه فضلاً وتعصباً في كل وقت. وكتب عزيزى بن عبد الملك في التاريخ حامداً الله ومصـلـيـا علـى مـحـمـد النبى وعلى آله وصـحـبـه وسـلـم وشــرف وكرم
A disgrace from the sprouts of the stupid anthropomorphists and a group of the dregs of the Hashwiyya, who are content with Islam in name and with knowledge by title. They were followed by commoners with no lineage or status. This curse among them became manifest in the markets, and none of his companions—may God multiply them—considered repelling foolishness with foolishness or evil with evil to be good. It is incumbent upon the overseer of the Muslims' affairs—he whose knowledge and justice have spread in the East and West, and whose command and prohibition have made the chests of friends and enemies submit, willingly or unwillingly—to support him, strengthen his arms, elevate his word, and debase the word of his lowly enemies. Patience is at the first shock, and this is the shock that has filled the hearts of the Shafi'is—may God multiply them—with distress and grief for years. That has now dissipated and been cleared in these days, supported, victorious, eternal, Nizamiyya, Qawwamiyya, 'Alamiyya, 'Adiliyya—may God support and elevate it. Its completion depends on the decisive victorious command from him, for in one branch of his care, support, and word for the religion whose folds He has extended, there is sufficient and effective. The planter must tend his planting with excellence and zeal at all times. 'Aziz ibn 'Abd al-Malik wrote in the date, praising God, and praying upon Muhammad the Prophet and his family and companions, and blessing and honoring.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a rhetorical condemnation of the anthropomorphist (mujassima) and Hashwiyya groups. The author begins by calling them a 'disgrace' and 'dregs', indicating their low status and deviation. He notes that they are merely nominal Muslims and scholars in name only. They are followed by ignorant commoners, and their corrupt beliefs have become public. The author then turns to address the ruler (likely Nizam al-Mulk), praising his widespread justice and authority. He insists that the ruler must support the righteous scholars and act decisively against the enemies of the religion. The 'first shock' refers to the initial impact of the fitna, which has now been resolved with the ruler's intervention. The passage ends with the scribe's signature.

Key Terms
المجسمة
الحشوية
أصحاب الشافعى
النظامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Hashwiyya were completely outside Islam or heretics to be excommunicated.
Correction: Ibn Asakir does not excommunicate them; he accuses them of being content with Islam in name only, implying they are nominal Muslims whose ignorance is harmful but not necessarily outside the fold.

Checkpoint
What does the author accuse the Hashwiyya of regarding their relationship with Islam?
A) Rejecting Islam entirely
B) Being content with Islam in name only
C) Being excellent scholars
D) Following the Shafi'i school

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir uses sharp rhetoric to condemn nominal Muslims and calls on the ruler to actively defend true Islamic teachings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you, like the Hashwiyya, content with the name of Islam and titles of knowledge, but empty of their substance? Examine your daily actions: do they reflect the reality of faith or just a label?
?
Ibn Asakir calls the ruler to actively defend the truth. In your own sphere of influence—your family, workplace, community—are you actively supporting true Islamic teachings, or do you remain passive while error spreads around you?
?
The Shafi'is endured years of grief before the fitna dissipated. What trial of faith have you been enduring in silence? Will you continue to wait passively, or will you step forward to support the truth with patience and action?

The Suppression of the Hashwiyya Fitna
Ibn Asakir narrates the suppression of the Hashwiyya fitna through the efforts of scholars and Nizam al-Mulk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical fitna involving the Hashwiyya and how the scholars, with the support of Nizam al-Mulk, suppressed it, leading to the vindication of the Ahl al-Sunna.

Core Idea
The fitna of the Hashwiyya was suppressed through combined scholarly and political action.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin recounts a pivotal episode in the defense of Sunni orthodoxy. It narrates how the excesses of the Hashwiyya—a group who barely understood hadith—forced the great scholars to seek intervention from the ruler Nizam al-Mulk. The story unfolds with conflicts, reconciliation, and ultimately the triumph of the Ahl al-Sunna. As you read, pay attention to the roles of the key figures and the sequence of events.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the overall story. Notice the key figures: Hashwiyya, Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, Nizam al-Mulk, al-Sharif Abu Ja'far.
2
Identify the main conflict
The Hashwiyya's fitna and the response of the scholars. Note the two phases: initial appeal to Nizam al-Mulk (469 AH) and later slander and second appeal (470 AH).
3
Understand the resolution
How did Nizam al-Mulk respond each time? What happened to al-Sharif Abu Ja'far? How did the Hashwiyya become suppressed?
4
Reflect on the outcome
The passage ends with the relief of Ahl al-Sunna and a reminder that all matters return to God. Consider the lesson's significance for Sunni identity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما طفح كيل فتن الحشوية الذين لا يكادون يفقهون حديثا اضطراً كابر العلماء المعروفون بكمال الهدوء والتؤدة والاناة إلى قمع فتنتهم بالسعى لدى ولى الأمر سعياً حثيثا ورفع الإمام أبو إسحق الشيرازي وأصحابه هذا المحضر إلى نظام الملك منتصرين للشيخ أبى نصر بن القشیری فعاد جواب نظام الملك إلى فخر الدولة وإلى الإمام أبي إسحق بانكار ما وقع والتشديد على خصوم ابن القشيري وذلك سنة تسع وستين وأربعمائة فسكن الحال ثم أخذ الشريف أبو جعفر بن أبي موسى – وهو شيخ الحنابلة إذ ذاك - وجماعته يتكلمون في الشيخ أبي إسحق ويبلغونه الأذى بالسنتهم فأمر الخليفة بجمعهم والصلح بينهم بعدما ثارت بينهم فتنة هائلة قتل فيها نحو من عشرين قتيلا فلما وقع الصلح وسكن الأمر أخذ الحنابلة يشيعون أن الشيح أبا إسحق تبرأ من مذهب الأشعرى فغضب الشيخ لذلك غضبا لم يصل أحد إلى تسكينه حتى كتب إلى نظام الملك يشكو أهل الفتن فعاد الجواب في سنة سبعين وأربعمائة إلى الشيخ باستجلاب خاطره وتعظيمه والأمر بتأدية الذين أثاروا الفتنة وبان يسجن الشريف أبو جعفر فهداً الحال وسكن جاش الشيخ وانقمعت الحشوية بعد أن تنفس أهل السنة الصعداء وإلى الله عاقبة الأمور
When the measure of the fitna of the Hashwiyya—who hardly understand any hadith—overflowed, the great scholars known for complete calm, deliberation, and forbearance were forced to suppress their fitna by diligently seeking the ruler. Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi and his companions raised this document to Nizam al-Mulk, supporting Sheikh Abu Nasr ibn al-Qushayri. The response of Nizam al-Mulk came to Fakhr al-Dawla and to Imam Abu Ishaq, rejecting what had occurred and emphasizing severity against the opponents of Ibn al-Qushayri. That was in the year 469 AH, and the situation calmed down. Then al-Sharif Abu Ja'far ibn Abi Musa—who was the head of the Hanbalis at that time—and his group began to speak about Sheikh Abu Ishaq and harmed him with their tongues. The Caliph ordered them to be gathered and reconciled after a terrible fitna had erupted between them in which about twenty people were killed. When reconciliation occurred and the matter settled, the Hanbalis began to spread that Sheikh Abu Ishaq had disavowed the Ash'ari school. The Sheikh became angry with an anger that no one could calm until he wrote to Nizam al-Mulk complaining about the people of fitna. The response came in the year 470 AH to the Sheikh, seeking to please him, exalting him, and ordering the punishment of those who had stirred the fitna, and that al-Sharif Abu Ja'far be imprisoned. The situation calmed, the Sheikh's agitation subsided, and the Hashwiyya were suppressed after the Ahl al-Sunna breathed a sigh of relief. And to God is the outcome of all matters.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative recounting the suppression of the Hashwiyya fitna. It describes how the scholars, led by Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, appealed to Nizam al-Mulk, who responded by rebuking the opponents of Ibn al-Qushayri. Later, the Hanbali leader Abu Ja'far and his followers slandered al-Shirazi, leading to a violent conflict with twenty deaths. After a reconciliation, the Hanbalis falsely claimed that al-Shirazi had abandoned Ash'arism. This angered al-Shirazi, who again appealed to Nizam al-Mulk, resulting in the imprisonment of Abu Ja'far and the suppression of the Hashwiyya. The passage ends with the relief of the Ahl al-Sunna and a reminder that all matters return to God.

Key Terms
الحشوية
نظام الملك
أبو إسحق الشيرازي
الحنابلة
الأشعرى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The fitna was purely theological.
Correction: The fitna involved political and personal conflicts, as the scholars appealed to the ruler and there was violence.

Checkpoint

B) Fakhr al-Dawla

D) Nizam al-Mulk

Key Takeaway
The Hashwiyya fitna was suppressed through the intervention of political authority, vindicating the Ash'ari scholars and bringing relief to Ahl al-Sunna.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This narrative shows scholars initially patient, then forced to take action. Think of a conflict in your own life where you remained silent or patient—did it eventually require action? Are you avoiding necessary confrontation right now out of false forbearance?
?
The Hanbalis spread a rumor that Abu Ishaq had abandoned his school. Have you ever been the victim of a false accusation or spread a rumor about someone else? How does this story challenge you to guard your tongue and verify news before speaking?
?
The caliph ordered reconciliation after violence claimed twenty lives. Is there a relationship in your life that has been damaged by heated disagreement? Are you willing to take the first step toward reconciliation, even if you feel you are in the right?

The Fitnah of the Hashwiyya and Its Suppression
Narrative of conflict between Ash'aris and Hashwiyya in Baghdad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical conflict between the Ash'aris and the Hashwiyya in 5th century Baghdad and how it was resolved through political intervention.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari scholars used political authority to suppress the fitnah of the Hashwiyya.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari recounts a period of intense conflict between the Ash'ari scholars and their literalist opponents, the Hashwiyya/Hanbalites, in Baghdad. It shows how the scholars eventually turned to the Seljuk vizier Nizam al-Mulk to suppress the fitnah and restore order. Read on to see how the events unfolded.

Guided Path
1
Read the historical narrative
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the story unfold naturally.
Pay attention to the sequence of events and the parties involved.
2
Identify the main parties
Notice the groups mentioned: the Hashwiyya, the Hanabilah (led by al-Sharif Abu Ja'far), and the Ash'ari scholars (Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, Ibn al-Qushayri). Also note the political authorities: the Caliph and Nizam al-Mulk.
3
Trace the escalation
Observe how the conflict escalates from verbal attacks to physical violence (20 people killed) and how political intervention is needed multiple times.
The first intervention calmed things temporarily; the second was more severe.
4
Reflect on the outcome
Consider what the resolution—imprisonment of the Hanbali leader and suppression of the Hashwiyya—says about the relationship between theology and politics in this period.
The Ash'aris gained relief through state power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما طفح كيل فتن الحشوية الذين لا يكادون يفقهون حديثا اضطراً كابر العلماء المعروفون بكمال الهدوء والتؤدة والاناة إلى قمع فتنتهم بالسعى لدى ولى الأمر سعياً حثيثا ورفع الإمام أبو إسحق الشيرازي وأصحابه هذا المحضر إلى نظام الملك منتصرين للشيخ أبى نصر بن القشیری فعاد جواب نظام الملك إلى فخر الدولة وإلى الإمام أبي إسحق بانكار ما وقع والتشديد على خصوم ابن القشيري وذلك سنة تسع وستين وأربعمائة فسكن الحال ثم أخذ الشريف أبو جعفر بن أبي موسى – وهو شيخ الحنابلة إذ ذاك - وجماعته يتكلمون في الشيخ أبي إسحق ويبلغونه الأذى بالسنتهم فأمر الخليفة بجمعهم والصلح بينهم بعدما ثارت بينهم فتنة هائلة قتل فيها نحو من عشرين قتيلا فلما وقع الصلح وسكن الأمر أخذ الحنابلة يشيعون أن الشيح أبا إسحق تبرأ من مذهب الأشعرى فغضب الشيخ لذلك غضبا لم يصل أحد إلى تسكينه حتى كتب إلى نظام الملك يشكو أهل الفتن فعاد الجواب في سنة سبعين وأربعمائة إلى الشيخ باستجلاب خاطره وتعظيمه والأمر بتأديب الذين أثاروا الفتنة وبان يسجن الشريف أبو جعفر فهداً الحال وسكن جاش الشيخ وانقمعت الحشوية بعد أن تنفس أهل السنة الصعداء وإلى الله عاقبة الأمور.
And when the measure of the fitnah of the Hashwiyya overflowed—those who scarcely understand a hadith—the great scholars known for complete calm, deliberateness, and forbearance were forced to suppress their fitnah by striving earnestly before the ruler. Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi and his companions raised this petition to Nizam al-Mulk, supporting Shaykh Abu Nasr ibn al-Qushayri. The response of Nizam al-Mulk came to Fakhr al-Dawla and to Imam Abu Ishaq, condemning what had occurred and being severe against the opponents of Ibn al-Qushayri, and that was in the year four hundred and sixty-nine (469 AH). So the situation calmed. Then al-Sharif Abu Ja'far ibn Abi Musa—who was the leader of the Hanabilah at that time—and his group began to speak about Shaykh Abu Ishaq and caused him harm with their tongues. So the Caliph ordered them to be gathered and reconciliation between them after a tremendous fitnah arose among them in which about twenty people were killed. When reconciliation occurred and the matter settled, the Hanabilah began to spread that Shaykh Abu Ishaq had disavowed the Ash'ari school. The Shaykh became angry with such anger that no one could calm him until he wrote to Nizam al-Mulk complaining of the people of the fitnah. The response came in the year four hundred and seventy (470 AH) to the Shaykh, mollifying him and honoring him, and ordering the punishment of those who had stirred up the fitnah, and that al-Sharif Abu Ja'far should be imprisoned. So the situation calmed, the Shaykh's agitation subsided, and the Hashwiyya were suppressed after the Ahl al-Sunnah breathed sighs of relief. And to God is the end of all matters.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative describing the fitnah (conflict) instigated by the Hashwiyya, a group of literalist hadith-folk often identified with the Hanbalites who opposed Ash'ari theology. The author begins by characterizing the Hashwiyya as those who scarcely understand a hadith, implying their ignorance. The great scholars, despite their calm nature, were forced to act. They, under the leadership of Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, submitted a petition to the vizier Nizam al-Mulk in support of Shaykh Abu Nasr ibn al-Qushayri (an Ash'ari). Nizam al-Mulk responded in 469 AH by condemning the opposition to Ibn al-Qushayri, which temporarily calmed the situation. However, al-Sharif Abu Ja'far ibn Abi Musa, the Hanbali leader, and his associates verbally abused Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi. The Caliph intervened, ordering a gathering to reconcile them, but not before a huge fitnah erupted in which about twenty people died. After reconciliation, the Hanbalis spread a rumor that Abu Ishaq had renounced Ash'arism, which enraged him. His anger could not be assuaged until he wrote to Nizam al-Mulk, who in 470 AH sent a response that honored Abu Ishaq, ordered the punishment of the instigators, and the imprisonment of al-Sharif Abu Ja'far. This led to the suppression of the Hashwiyya and relief for the Ahl al-Sunnah (referring to Ash'aris). The narrative ends with a pious phrase. The passage illustrates the political and social dimensions of theological conflicts in the 5th century AH.

Key Terms
فتنة
الحشوية
الحنابلة
نظام الملك
أبو إسحق الشيرازي
أبو نصر بن القشيري
أهل السنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Hashwiyya are identical to all Hanbalites.
Correction: While the Hashwiyya are often associated with Hanbalites, they are a subset known for extreme literalism; not all Hanbalites were Hashwiyya.

Checkpoint
What was the outcome of Nizam al-Mulk's response in 470 AH?
A) Al-Sharif Abu Ja'far was imprisoned
B) Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi was exiled
C) The Hashwiyya were given official recognition
D) A new school of thought was established

Key Takeaway
This narrative shows how political authority was used to suppress theological conflict in medieval Baghdad, highlighting the interdependence of religion and state in the 5th century AH.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When the Hanabilah spread a false rumor about Abu Ishaq, he became furiously angry and complained to the authorities. Is there a falsehood about you or your beliefs that you have let slide because confronting it was uncomfortable? Would you be willing to escalate to protect the truth, even if it meant someone else's imprisonment?
?
The great scholars were forced to act only after the fitnah overflowed. Examine your own life: have you tolerated small theological compromises or false teachings around you, waiting until they caused harm? What would it take for you to speak up sooner, even if it costs you your reputation for calmness?
?
The Ahl al-Sunnah breathed sighs of relief when the Hashwiyya were suppressed. Reflect on the beliefs you hold dear: what 'Hashwiyya'—any form of ignorant literalism or falsehood—needs to be suppressed in your own heart? Are you willing to ask God to uproot it, even if the process is painful?

Defense of Ash'ari School Against Majority Argument
Refutation of the claim that majority rejection invalidates Ash'ari school

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the argument from majority rejection does not invalidate the Ash'ari school, and how the author refutes it using the criterion of knowledge and insight.

Core Idea
Truth is not determined by majority but by people of knowledge and insight.

This lesson presents a classic objection against the Ash'ari school: that most people do not follow al-Ash'ari, implying his way is wrong. The author refutes this by arguing that the common majority is not a measure of truth; rather, the people of knowledge and insight are the true guides, and the Ash'aris are numerous among them. The passage also invokes Quranic reminders that the faithful are often few and a wise saying from Fudayl ibn Iyad.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the objection that the great multitude does not follow al-Ash'ari, and how it presents this as evidence against his school.
The objection is a common rhetorical move: majority rejection implies falsehood.
2
Identify the author's refutation
Find the key phrase 'لا عبرة بكثرة العوام' (no heed is given to the multitude of the common people). Understand that the author shifts the criterion from quantity to quality—only people of knowledge and insight matter.
3
Examine the Quranic support
Look at the two Quranic verses cited: 'But few believed with him' (Hud 11:40) and 'Few of My servants are grateful' (Saba 34:13). They show that truth often belongs to a minority.
4
Reflect on Fudayl ibn Iyad's saying
Read the narration from Fudayl: 'Do not feel lonely on the paths of guidance because of the fewness of their people, and do not be deceived by the multitude of the perishing.' This reinforces the lesson.
5
Consider the concluding warning
The author ends with a strong statement: anyone who criticizes the Ash'ari party after reading this book is a slanderer. This shows the severity of spreading false claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل إن الجم الغفير في سائر الأزمان وأكثر العامة في جميع البلدان لا يقتدون بالأشعري ولا يقلدونه ولا يرون مذهبه ولا يعتقدونه وهم السواد الأعظم، وسبيلهم السبيل الأقوم قيل لا عبرة بكثرة العوام ولا التفات إلى الجهلاء الغتماء وإنما الاعتبار بأرباب العلم والاقتداء بأصحاب البصيرة والفهم وأولئك في أصحابه أكثر ممن سواهم ولهم الفضل والتقدم على من عداهم على أن الله عز وجل قال ( وما آمن معه إلا قليل) وقال عز من قائل ( وقليل من عبادي الشكور ) وقد قال الفضيل بن عياض رحمه الله ما أخبرنا أبو القسم زاهر بن طاهر فيما قرأته عليه عن أبي بكر أحمد بن الحسين الحافظ قال أخبرنا أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الحافظ قال سمعت أبا إسحق المزكي يقول حدثني أبو القسم عبد الرحمن بن محمد بن الحسن الواعظ قال حدثنا محمد بن أبي حمزة المروزي عن أحمد بن أيوب المطوعي قال قال الحسن بن زياد كلمة سمعتها من الفضيل بن عياض قال الفضيل لا تستوحش طرق الهدى لقلة أهلها ولا تغترن بكثرة الهالكين فمن ذم بعد وقوفه على كتابي هذا حزب الأشعري فهو مفتر كذاب عليه ما على المفترى
If it is said that the great multitude in all ages and most of the common people in all countries do not follow al-Ash'ari, nor imitate him, nor see his madhhab, nor believe in it, and they are the vast majority, and their way is the most upright—it is said: No heed is given to the multitude of the common people, nor attention to the ignorant and foolish, but rather consideration is given to the people of knowledge and following to those of insight and understanding. And those among his companions are more than others, and they possess virtue and precedence over those other than them. Moreover, God Almighty said: 'But few believed with him' and 'Few of My servants are grateful.' And Fudayl ibn Iyad, may God have mercy on him, said—and we were informed by Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir from what I read to him from Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Hafiz, who said: Abu Abdallah Muhammad ibn Abdallah al-Hafiz informed us, he said: I heard Abu Ishaq al-Muzakki say: Abu al-Qasim Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Wa'iz narrated to me, he said: Muhammad ibn Abi Hamza al-Marwazi narrated to us from Ahmad ibn Ayyub al-Mutawwi'i, who said: Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad said: I heard a word from Fudayl ibn Iyad, who said: 'Do not feel lonely on the paths of guidance because of the fewness of their people, and do not be deceived by the multitude of the perishing.' So whoever criticizes, after reading my book, the party of al-Ash'ari, is a slanderer and liar; upon him is what is upon the slanderer.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer in defense of the Ash'ari school. The objection claims that the majority of people do not follow al-Ash'ari, implying that his way is incorrect. The answer refutes this by arguing that the majority of common people is not a criterion for truth; rather, the people of knowledge and insight are to be followed, and the Ash'aris are numerous among them. It cites Quranic verses (Hud 11:40, Saba 34:13) and a saying of Fudayl ibn Iyad to support that truth is often with a minority. The author concludes that anyone who criticizes the Ash'ari party after reading this book is a slanderer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the truth of a religious school is determined by the number of followers among common people.
Correction: The author argues that truth is determined by the people of knowledge and insight, not by the multitude of the ignorant. He provides Quranic and traditional support.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the correct criterion for following a school?
A) The multitude of followers
B) The authority of people of knowledge and insight
C) The popularity among common people
D) The consensus of all Muslims

Key Takeaway
The truth of a religious school is not measured by the number of followers among the common people, but by the weight of knowledge and insight among its adherents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you choose a teacher or a scholar to follow in religious matters, do you tend to pick the most popular one or the one with the most convincing evidence, even if they are not widely accepted? What is one specific step you can take this week to ensure you are following knowledge rather than crowd?
?
Fudayl ibn Iyad said, 'Do not feel lonely on the paths of guidance because of the fewness of their people.' Is there a truth you believe in—about God, worship, or morality—that makes you feel isolated from those around you? How can you strengthen your resolve to stay on that path?
?
The author warns that criticizing the Ash'ari party after reading this book is slander. Have you ever dismissed a legitimate Islamic school or opinion simply because it was not mainstream? Before you judge another scholar or madhhab, what can you do to ensure you are not speaking out of ignorance?

Three Fatwas Against Cursing and Takfir of Ash'aris
Legal opinions condemning the cursing and takfir of Ash'aris

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that a number of prominent Hanafi imams issued fatwas declaring that cursing and declaring takfir on the Ash'aris is an innovation that must be disciplined, and that the Ash'aris are defenders of the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Cursing and takfir of Ash'aris is an innovation that requires discipline.

This passage presents a legal question and three authoritative fatwas from major Hanafi imams of the 5th-6th centuries AH. The question concerns a group that gathered to curse and declare the Ash'aris disbelievers. The imams' responses uniformly condemn this act as an innovation and mandate disciplinary action, while also affirming the Ash'aris' role as defenders of the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Read the question and identify the issue
Read the opening question carefully. Understand what the asker wants: a ruling on people who curse Ash'aris and declare them kuffar.
Notice the respectful address to the imams.
2
Study the first fatwa by al-Damaghani
Al-Damaghani's answer rules that such action is innovation (bid'a) and impermissible. The ruler must discipline the perpetrators.
He uses the term 'yabtadi' (he has innovated).
3
Study the second fatwa by al-Firuzabadi
Al-Firuzabadi defends the Ash'aris as 'the notables of the Sunnah' and defenders of Sharia. Attacking them is attacking Ahl al-Sunnah. The ruler must discipline.
Note the phrase 'a'yan al-sunna' (pillars of the Sunnah).
4
Note the third fatwa and the author's praise
Al-Shashi simply agrees. Then Ibn 'Asakir praises each imam's status: al-Damaghani as 'second Abu Hanifa', al-Firuzabadi as widely renowned, and al-Shashi as known to all.
This praise reinforces the authority of their fatwas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد وجدت في جزء بخط بعض الثقات سؤالا يتعقبه ما أذكره بعد من الأجوبة نقلته على نصه ونسخته ليقف عليه من ينتفع بمعرفته، وهو بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم ما قول السادة الجلة الأئمة الفقهاء أحسن الله توفيقهم ورضي عنهم في قوم اجتمعوا على لعن فرقة الأشعري وتكفيرهم ما الذي يجب عليهم في هذا القول يفتونا في ذلك منعمين مثابين إن شاء الله. الجواب وبالله التوفيق أن كل من أقدم على لعن فرقة من المسلمين وتكفيرهم فقد ابتدع وارتكب مالا يجوز الإقدام عليه وعلى الناظر في الأمور أعز الله أنصاره الإنكار عليه وتأديبه بما يرتدع هو وأمثاله عن ارتكاب مثله. وكتب محمد بن علي الدامغاني، وبعده الجواب وبالله التوفيق أن الأشعرية أعيان السنة ونصار الشريعة انتصبوا للرد على المبتدعة من القدرية والرافضة وغيرهم فمن طعن فيهم فقد طعن على أهل السنة وإذا رفع أمر من يفعل ذلك إلى الناظر في أمر المسلمين وجب عليه تأديبه بما يرتدع به كل أحد. وكتب إبراهيم بن علي الفيروزبادي. وبعده جوابي مثله. وكتب محمد بن أحمد الشاشي فهذه أجوبة هؤلاء الأئمة الذين كانوا في عصرهم علماء الأمة، فأما قاضي القضاة أبو عبد الله الحنيفي الدامغاني فكان يقال له في عصره أبو حنيفة الثاني وأما الشيخ الإمام أبو إسحق فقد طبق ذكر فضله الآفاق وأما الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر الشاشي فلا يخفى محله على منتهى في العلم ولا ناشي
And I found in a volume in the handwriting of some reliable person a question followed by the answers that I will mention after, transmitted as its text and copy, so that whoever benefits from its knowledge may examine it. It is: 'In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. What is the saying of the noble masters, the imams, the jurists—may God improve their success and be pleased with them—concerning a people who have gathered to curse the group of al-Ash'ari and declare them disbelievers: what is obligatory upon them in this statement? Give us a fatwa regarding that, rewarded and recompensed, God willing.' The answer: 'And with God is success. Whoever initiates cursing a group of Muslims and declaring them disbelievers has innovated and committed what is not permissible to initiate. And upon the overseer of affairs—may God strengthen his supporters—is to denounce him and discipline him in a way that he and his likes desist from committing the like.' Written by Muhammad ibn Ali al-Damaghani. And after it, the answer: 'And with God is success. The Ash'aris are the notables of the Sunnah and the defenders of the Sharia; they stood up to refute the innovators among the Qadaris, Rafidis, and others. So whoever disparages them has disparaged the people of the Sunnah. And if the matter of one who does that is raised to the overseer of the Muslims' affairs, it is obligatory upon him to discipline him in a way that everyone desists.' Written by Ibrahim ibn Ali al-Firuzabadi. And after it, 'My answer is the same.' Written by Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Shashi. So these are the answers of these imams who were in their time the scholars of the nation. As for the Chief Judge Abu Abdallah al-Hanafi al-Damaghani, he was called in his time 'the second Abu Hanifa'. As for Shaykh Imam Abu Ishaq, his virtue spread to the horizons. As for Shaykh Imam Abu Bakr al-Shashi, his status is not hidden from the one at the end in knowledge nor a beginner.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage presents a legal question and three fatwas from prominent Hanafi imams regarding those who curse and declare Takfir on the Ash'aris. The first answer by al-Damaghani states that such action is innovation and impermissible, and the ruler must discipline such people. The second by al-Firuzabadi emphasizes that the Ash'aris are defenders of Sunnah and Sharia, so attacking them is attacking Ahl al-Sunnah, and the ruler must discipline. The third by al-Shashi concurs. The author then praises the three imams, highlighting their high status.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think it is permissible to curse and declare takfir on Ash'aris because they are seen as misguided.
Correction: The fatwas clarify that this is an innovation and impermissible; the Ash'aris are defenders of the Sunnah.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad ibn Ali al-Damaghani, what is the ruling on someone who curses a group of Muslims and declares them disbelievers?
A) It is permissible if they are innovators
B) It is an innovation and impermissible, requiring discipline
C) It is a minor sin
D) It is only allowed if the group is known to be disbelievers

Key Takeaway
Prominent Hanafi imams issued fatwas ruling that cursing and takfir of Ash'aris is a forbidden innovation, and the Ash'aris are esteemed defenders of the Sunnah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever judged or spoken negatively about a group of Muslims because of their theological label? What would these imams say to you, and how will you change your speech and attitude starting today?
?
The fatwas demand discipline for those who curse and takfir. If you have ever casually uttered takfir or criticism of Ash'aris (or any Sunni group), will you repent and publicly clarify your stance as an act of accountability before God?
?
These imams were known for their deep knowledge and piety. Do you seek knowledge to be like them—defending the Sunnah and uniting Muslims—or do you use partial knowledge to divide? What step will you take this week to seek correct knowledge and avoid divisive speech?

The Objection from Early Scholars: Is Kalam Blameworthy?
Presents objection citing Abu Yusuf's condemnation of kalam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classical objection against kalam based on the narration of Abu Yusuf and the need for a response from defenders of kalam.

Core Idea
Early scholars condemned kalam as innovation—can mutakallimun still be praiseworthy?

This lesson presents a serious objection that challenges the praise of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari as a mutakallim. The objector cites the criticism of kalam by leading scholars like Imam al-Shafi'i and a narration from Abu Yusuf that equates seeking religion through kalam with becoming a zindiq. Understanding this objection is crucial for appreciating how later theologians like Imam Ibn Asakir defended kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the objector frames the argument: the praise amounts only to being a mutakallim, which is not praiseworthy according to Ahl al-Sunnah.
The objector uses a rhetorical question to force a response.
2
Identify the key authorities cited
Note the mention of 'scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah' and the specific reference to Imam al-Shafi'i, who is said to have strongly condemned mutakallimun.
The objector appeals to the founder of the Shafi'i school, to which the author is affiliated.
3
Examine the narration from Abu Yusuf
The narration lists three pursuits leading to ruin: seeking religion via kalam leads to zandaqah, seeking wealth via alchemy leads to bankruptcy, and narrating strange hadiths leads to lying.
The first part directly condemns the very subject of the praise.
4
Consider the transmission and authenticity
The author notes that the narration is transmitted by al-Tabari from Abu Yusuf, but others transmit it as Abu Yusuf's own statement. This raises questions about its strength and meaning.
The author implies the statement may be Abu Yusuf's personal opinion, not a prophetic hadith.
5
Reflect on the challenge posed
This objection places the author in a difficult position: how can he praise al-Ash'ari as a mutakallim if such strong condemnations exist? The answer will follow in subsequent lessons.
This lesson sets up the need for a defense of kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل غاية ما تمدحون به أبا الحسن أن تثبتوا أنه متكلم وتدلونا على أنه بالمعرفة برسوم الجدل متوسم ولا فخر في ذلك عند العلماء من ذوى التسنن والاتباع لأنهم يرون أن من تشاغل بذلك من أهل الابتداع وقد حفظ عن غير واحد من علماء الإسلام عيب المتكلمين وذم الكلام ولو لم يذمهم غير الشافعي رحمه الله لكفى ، فإنه قد بالغ في ذمهم وأوضح حالهم وشفى وأنتم تنتسبون إلى مذهبه فهلا أقتديتم في ذلك به فمما جاء في ذلك ما أخبرنا الشيخ أبو عبد الله الحسين بن عبد الملك ابن الحسين الخلال باصبهان قال أخبرنا أبو طاهر أحمد بن محمود بن أحمد الثقفى قال أخبرنا أبو بكر محمد بن إبراهيم بن المقرى ، قال ثنا مفضل بن محمد الجندى قال حدثنا إسحق بن إبراهيم الطبرى ، قال ثنا أبو يوسف القاضي عن مجالد عن الشعبي ، أنه قال من طلب الدين بالكلام تزندق ومن طلب المال بالكيمياء أفلس ومن حدث بغرائب الحديث كذب. هكذا رواها هذا الطبرى عن أبي يوسف ورواها غيره عن أبى يوسف من قوله ، وهو أشبه بالصواب.
If it is said: The utmost you praise Abu al-Hasan for is that you affirm he is a mutakallim and you point out to us that he is distinguished by knowledge of the rules of debate, and there is no pride in that according to the scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, because they consider that whoever occupies himself with that is among the people of innovation, and it has been preserved from more than one of the scholars of Islam the criticism of the mutakallimun and the blame of kalam. If none other than al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, had blamed them, it would have sufficed, for he went to great lengths in blaming them, clarified their condition, and gave full explanation. And you claim to follow his school, so why do you not follow him in that? Among what has come regarding that is what the shaykh Abu Abdullah al-Husayn ibn Abd al-Malik ibn al-Husayn al-Khallal in Isbahan informed us, he said: Abu Tahir Ahmad ibn Mahmud ibn Ahmad al-Thaqafi informed us, he said: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn al-Muqri' informed us, he said: Mufaddal ibn Muhammad al-Jundi narrated to us, he said: Ishaq ibn Ibrahim al-Tabari narrated to us, he said: Abu Yusuf al-Qadi narrated to us from Mujalid, from al-Sha'bi, that he said: Whoever seeks religion through kalam becomes a zindiq; whoever seeks wealth through alchemy becomes bankrupt; and whoever narrates strange hadiths lies. Thus did al-Tabari narrate it from Abu Yusuf, and others narrated it from Abu Yusuf as his own statement, and that is more likely correct.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage begins by presenting an objection against the author's praise of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari as a mutakallim. The objector argues that scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah criticize kalam and its practitioners, considering them innovators, and that even al-Shafi'i, to whose school the author claims allegiance, strongly condemned kalam. The objector then cites a specific narration from Abu Yusuf via al-Sha'bi: 'Whoever seeks religion through kalam becomes a zindiq; whoever seeks wealth through alchemy becomes bankrupt; and whoever narrates strange hadiths lies.' The author notes that this narration is transmitted by al-Tabari from Abu Yusuf, and others transmit it as Abu Yusuf's own statement, which is more likely correct. The purpose is to challenge the legitimacy of kalam and the author's glorification of al-Ash'ari in light of early scholarly condemnation.

Key Terms
متكلم
كلام
أهل البدع
تزندق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this narration condemns all forms of kalam absolutely.
Correction: Later scholars restrict it to the kalam of innovators, not the disciplined theology of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Checkpoint
According to the narration from Abu Yusuf, what happens to one who seeks religion through kalam?
A) He becomes a zindiq
B) He becomes bankrupt
C) He tells lies
D) He becomes a scholar

Key Takeaway
This passage presents a powerful objection against kalam using early scholarly authority, which later theologians had to address.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever engaged in theological debates where your intention was not to seek truth but to win an argument? How does the warning of al-Sha'bi about seeking religion through kalam challenge your motivation?
?
The objector cites the authority of early scholars like al-Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf. When you encounter a hadith or statement that seems to condemn a practice you value, do you immediately reject it, or do you pause to understand the context and intent? Which response leads to deeper faith?
?
Abu Yusuf warns that seeking religion through kalam can lead to zandaqah (heresy). In your own pursuit of Islamic knowledge, where do you draw the line between beneficial understanding and harmful speculation? Are there questions about Allah that you are content to not know?

Al-Shafi'i's Condemnation of Kalam
Cites multiple narrations of al-Shafi'i condemning kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the severity of al-Shafi'i's condemnation of kalam as transmitted through two complete narrations, and the importance of considering context when interpreting such statements.

Core Idea
Al-Shafi'i likened kalam to all sins except shirk—a shocking condemnation.

This lesson presents two powerful narrations from Imam al-Shafi'i that are among the harshest criticisms of kalam in Islamic tradition. As we read these, it is important to see how these statements have been understood and reconciled with the later development of kalam for defending orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read the two complete narrations
Carefully read the first two narrations with their chains. Notice the wording 'better to be afflicted with everything Allah has forbidden except shirk' and 'no one engaged in kalam and succeeded'.
The third narration is incomplete, ending mid-sentence.
2
Reflect on the severity of the language
Consider why al-Shafi'i would place kalam above all sins except shirk. This indicates a very strong view.
3
Consider the context and transmission
These statements were transmitted by later scholars. Ask yourself: what was the historical context of al-Shafi'i's time? How did later Ash'aris respond?
The common misunderstanding is that this justifies complete rejection of theology, but many later scholars engaged in kalam for defense.
4
Note the incomplete third narration
The page ends mid-chain. This highlights that the author (Ibn Asakir) may have more to say in subsequent pages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قول الشافعى فيه فأخبرنا الشيخ أبو الأعز قراتكين بن الأسعد الازجى قال أخبرنا أبو محمد الحسن بن علی بن محمد الجوهرى قال أنا أبو الحسن علي بن عبد العزيز بن مردك ، قال أنا أبو محمد عبد الرحمن بن أبي حاتم الرازي قال ثنا يونس بن عبد الأعلى المصرى ، قال سمعت الشافعي يقول لأن يبتلى المرء بكل ما نهى الله عنه سوى الشرك خير له من الكلام ، ولقد أطلعت من أهل الكلام على شي ما ظننت أن مسلما يقول ذلك . وأخبرنا قراتكين بن الأسعد قال أنا الحسن ابن على قال أنا على بن عبد العزيز قال أخبرنا عبد الرحمن بن أبي حاتم قال ثنا أحمد بن أصرم المزني من ولد عبد الله بن المغفل قال قال أبو ثور سمعت الشافعي يقول : ما تردى أحد في الكلام فأفلح ، وأخبرنا الشيخ الفقيه أبو الفتح نصر الله ابن محمد بن عبد القوى المصيصي بدمشق قال ، أنا أبو البركات أحمد ابن عبد الله بن على بن طاوس المقرى البغدادى بدمشق ، قال أخبرنا أبو القسم عبيد الله بن أحمد بن عثمان الصيرفى قال لنا أبو على الحسن بن الحسين بن حمكان الفقيه قال حدثنى الزبير بن عبد الواحد ، قال حدثني أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف الهروى بدمشق قال رأيت في كتاب عن أبي بكر محمد بن الجنيد صاحب أبى ثور قال سمعت أبا ثور يقول سمعت
As for the statement of al-Shafi'i regarding it, the shaykh Abu al-A'azz Qaratakin ibn al-As'ad al-Azaji informed us, he said: Abu Muhammad al-Hasan ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Jawhari informed us, he said: Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Abd al-Aziz ibn Mardak told us, he said: Abu Muhammad Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Hatim al-Razi told us, he said: Yunus ibn Abd al-A'la al-Misri narrated to us, he said: I heard al-Shafi'i say: 'It is better for a person to be afflicted with everything Allah has forbidden except shirk than to engage in kalam. Indeed, I have seen from the people of kalam things I never thought a Muslim would say.' And Qaratakin ibn al-As'ad informed us, he said: al-Hasan ibn Ali told us, he said: Ali ibn Abd al-Aziz told us, he said: Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Hatim informed us, he said: Ahmad ibn Asram al-Muzani from the descendants of Abdullah ibn al-Mughaffal narrated to us, he said: Abu Thawr said: I heard al-Shafi'i say: 'No one engaged in kalam and succeeded.' And the shaykh al-faqih Abu al-Fath Nasrallah ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Qawi al-Misisi in Damascus informed us, he said: Abu al-Barakat Ahmad ibn Abdullah ibn Ali ibn Tawus al-Muqri' al-Baghdadi in Damascus told us, he said: Abu al-Qasim Ubaydullah ibn Ahmad ibn Uthman al-Sayrafi informed us, he said: Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn al-Husayn ibn Hamkan al-Faqih told us, he said: al-Zubayr ibn Abd al-Wahid narrated to me, he said: Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Harawi in Damascus narrated to me, he said: I saw in a book from Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Junayd, the companion of Abu Thawr, he said: I heard Abu Thawr say: I heard
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage presents several strong condemnations of kalam attributed to al-Shafi'i through multiple chains. The first: 'It is better for a person to be afflicted with everything Allah has forbidden except shirk than to engage in kalam. Indeed, I have seen from the people of kalam things I never thought a Muslim would say.' The second: 'No one engaged in kalam and succeeded.' The third chain begins but is cut off at the end of the page. These statements are the most severe against kalam, and the author is likely preparing to address them in the following text (which is not included in this window). The purpose is to present the strongest evidence against the author's position, setting up a response. The chains show the care taken to transmit these sayings accurately.

Key Terms
الشافعي
الكلام
الشرك
أهل الكلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that al-Shafi'i's condemnation means all forms of theological reasoning are forbidden and that later Ash'ari theology is a deviation.
Correction: Al-Shafi'i's statements must be understood in their historical context, where 'kalam' often referred to speculative theology influenced by Greek philosophy and deviant sects. Later scholars, including Ash'aris, engaged in a disciplined form of kalam to defend orthodoxy, which was not the subject of al-Shafi'i's censure.

Checkpoint
According to the first narration from al-Shafi'i, what is better than engaging in kalam?
A) Being afflicted with everything Allah forbade except shirk
B) Being afflicted with shirk
C) Being silent
D) Being a zindiq

Key Takeaway
Al-Shafi'i's condemnations of kalam are extremely severe, equating it to near-shirk and declaring it a cause of failure, but these statements must be historically contextualized.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read al-Shafi'i's shocking statement that it is better to be afflicted with every sin except shirk than to engage in kalam. Do you take your own theological arguments and debates with others as seriously as he did? Are you willing to admit that sometimes you argue not for truth but for ego? What would you change about how you discuss religion after reading this?
?
Al-Shafi'i said he saw things from the people of kalam that he never thought a Muslim would say. Have you ever encountered or participated in theological discussions that crossed a line into disbelief? How does this warning affect your willingness to engage in or avoid such debates?
?
The narration declares that no one who engaged in kalam succeeded. If you have ever delved into theological debates, does this statement cause you to reflect on your own success in faith? What is more important to you: winning an argument or pleasing Allah? How will you prioritize your religious discussions from now on?

Al-Shafi'i's Censure of Kalam Applies Only to Innovators
Ibn Asakir defends kalam by contextualizing al-Shafi'i's condemnations as targeting innovators only.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that al-Shafi'i's harsh statements about kalam were specifically targeting the theological speculations of the Qadariyya and similar innovators, not the discipline of kalam itself.

Core Idea
Al-Shafi'i condemned only the kalam of innovators, not all theological reasoning.

In this lesson, we examine a collection of reports in which al-Shafi'i appears to condemn kalam severely. However, Ibn Asakir shows through contextual evidence that these condemnations were directed specifically at the Qadariyya and those who argued about predestination. Understanding this distinction is crucial for appreciating the value of orthodox kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the reports of al-Shafi'i's sayings
First, read the multiple reports where al-Shafi'i speaks harshly about kalam. Notice the strong language he uses.
2
Observe the context clues
Pay attention to the incident with al-Rabi' and the mention of Hafs al-Fard. These show that al-Shafi'i's anger was provoked by specific topics and people.
The report from al-Rabi' mentions people speaking about qadar (predestination).
3
Study Ibn Asakir's interpretation
Ibn Asakir directly explains that al-Shafi'i meant the kalam of the innovator who opposes legal evidence. He cites Zakariyya al-Saji's clarification that the forbiddance was about the kalam of the Qadariyya.
4
Connect to the overall argument
Understanding that this is a defense of kalam from a false accusation helps you see how Ibn Asakir reconciles apparent contradictions in the tradition.
This resolves the tension between al-Shafi'i's statements and the practice of later scholars who engaged in kalam.

Source Text
