The Truthful Scholar on Earth — Ibn Asakir's Refutation
Ibn Asakir refutes the opponent's claim about a truthful scholar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Asakir's refutation of the opponent's claim that the earth is never devoid of a truthful scholar, and his argument that the true scholars are those condemned by the opponent.

Core Idea
Ibn Asakir agrees with the principle but denies the opponent qualifies as that scholar.

The opponent asserts that Allah always leaves a truthful, wise scholar on earth to speak truth and repel falsehood. Ibn Asakir acknowledges this principle as true but turns it against the opponent: the opponent himself is not such a scholar, and the real scholars are those he has defamed. Let's examine the passage to see how this refutation works.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the opponent's claim and Ibn Asakir's initial agreement.
2
Identify the opponent's description
The opponent describes a truthful speaker and wise scholar who repels falsehood. Ibn Asakir agrees that such a person exists, but not the opponent.
3
Understand the turn
Ibn Asakir argues that the opponent is not among those scholars; rather, the scholars he has condemned are the true ones. This refutation uses the opponent's own statement against him.
The condemned scholars are likely the Ash'ari scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله ( أن الله عز وجل لا يخلى الأرض من قائل عليم وعالم حكيم يقول الحق ويدفع الباطل ، ولا يدع لذى بدعة قولا يعلو ولا أمراً . فقد صدق ولكن ليس هو ممن وصفه بهذه الصفة إذ لم يتحقق يسمو كونه من أهل العلم ولا من ذوى المعرفة ، ولكن هم العلماء الذين بالغ في ذمهم وأغرق لفرط جهله وسوء عقده في شتمهم وأما قوله ( لا معروف أفضل من السنة ولا منكر أشد من البدعة. فانظروا بعين التحقيق إلى مقالة هذا القرعة لتعلموا أهو أشد تسننا وأقوى في العلم تمكنا أم من أشتهرت ردوده على جميع المبتدعة من أصناف الخوارج وطوائف المتشيعة وانتشرت تصانيفه فى الابطال لمذاهب المعتزلة القدرية والإنكار على من يقول بأقوال المفوضة الجبرية والاصطلام لحجج المعطلة الجهمية والمحق لتعلقات المشبهة الجسمية من الكرامية والسالمية بالحجج السمعية والبراهين العقلية فإن اعتقد أن الرد على أصحاب البدع بدعة فقد تحقق كل ذي لب تسميتي إياه قرعة وإن اعتقد أن البدعة اعتقاد التنزيه والتوحيد والسنة القول بالتشبيه والميل إلى التقليد فبئس ما اعتقد وويل له مما تقلد ، وإن كان يبدع الأشعري رحمه الله في بعض المسائل الأدلة الاقلة فليذكر ما ابتدع فيه حتى نسمع ما عنده عليه من
As for his saying: 'Allah does not leave the earth devoid of a truthful speaker and a wise scholar who speaks the truth and repels falsehood, and does not leave for any innovator a statement that rises nor an affair.' He has spoken truthfully, but he is not among those described with this attribute, for he has not attained to be of the people of knowledge nor of the possessors of understanding. Rather, they are the scholars whom he has excessively condemned and drowned due to his extreme ignorance and bad belief in reviling them. And as for his saying: 'There is no known good better than the Sunnah, and no known evil more severe than bid'ah.' Look with the eye of verification at the statement of this bald man to know whether he is more strongly adhering to Sunnah and more firmly established in knowledge, or the one whose refutations against all innovators from the various branches of Khawarij and groups of Shia are famous, and whose books have spread in invalidating the schools of the Mu'tazila Qadariyya and in denouncing those who say the sayings of the Mufawwida Jabariyya, and in seizing the arguments of the Jahmiyya Mu'attila, and in proving the attachments of the Mujassima Mushabbiha from the Karamiyya and Salimiyya with scriptural evidences and rational proofs. If he believes that refuting the people of bid'ah is itself bid'ah, then every possessor of intellect has verified my calling him 'bald.' And if he believes that bid'ah is believing in transcendence and tawhid, and that Sunnah is saying anthropomorphism and inclining to blind imitation, then evil is what he believes, and woe to him from what he imitates. And if he declares al-Ash'ari an innovator in some issues of the few evidences, let him mention what he innovated so that we may hear what he has against him.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage refutes two more claims. First, the opponent says Allah never leaves the earth without a truthful wise scholar who repels falsehood. Ibn Asakir agrees with the principle but denies that the opponent qualifies as such a scholar. In fact, the opponent has condemned the real scholars. Second, the opponent asserts that no good is better than Sunnah and no evil worse than bid'ah. Ibn Asakir challenges the opponent's consistency: the opponent claims to uphold Sunnah, but al-Ash'ari and his followers are the ones who have actually refuted all innovating sects (Khawarij, Shia, Mu'tazila, Jabariyya, Jahmiyya, Mujassima, etc.). If the opponent thinks refuting innovators is bid'ah, then he is foolish. If he thinks that believing in tawhid (transcendence) is bid'ah and anthropomorphism is Sunnah, then he is ruined. If he accuses al-Ash'ari of innovating in some issues, let him specify.

بدعة
عالم
قائل عليم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Ibn Asakir say the opponent does not qualify as the truthful scholar?
A) Because the opponent does not speak the truth
B) Because the opponent has condemned the true scholars
C) Because the opponent is an innovator
D) Because the opponent lacks knowledge

Key Takeaway
The existence of a truthful scholar on earth is a divine promise, but the opponent's condemnation of true scholars disqualifies him from that description.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever spoken ill of a scholar or dismissed their teachings because of a personal disagreement? How does Ibn Asakir's description of the opponent's 'extreme ignorance and bad belief in reviling them' challenge you to examine the state of your own heart towards those who carry sacred knowledge?
?
The truthful scholar is defined by knowledge and understanding, not by attacks on others. Think of a recent conversation you had about religious matters: did you defend truth while respecting others, or did you condemn people? What would it take for you to embody the attribute of a truthful speaker without falling into the opponent's error?
?
Ibn Asakir says the opponent does not attain to be 'of the people of knowledge nor of the possessors of understanding.' Reflect on your own learning: are you truly seeking knowledge and understanding, or are you content with surface-level arguments that lead you to belittle those who differ? What one step can you take today to deepen your understanding before you speak?

Sunnah's Virtue and Bid'ah's Evil — Ibn Asakir's Challenge
Ibn Asakir defends al-Ash'ari by listing his refutations against various sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Asakir's argument that the opponent's claim about the superiority of Sunnah and evil of bid'ah is used to expose his inconsistency, and that al-Ash'ari's followers are the true defenders of Sunnah.

Core Idea
If refuting innovators is bid'ah, then the opponent stands condemned.

The opponent declares that no good surpasses the Sunnah and no evil surpasses bid'ah. Ibn Asakir immediately challenges him: if this is true, then the one who refutes all innovating sects (like al-Ash'ari) is the true adherent of Sunnah, while the opponent's condemnation of these refuters reveals his hypocrisy. The passage lists the various groups refuted by al-Ash'ari and ends with a conditional challenge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'وأما قوله (لا معروف أفضل من السنة...' and its translation. Notice the list of sects and the conditional statements.
2
List the sects refuted by al-Ash'ari
Identify the various groups mentioned: Khawarij, Shia, Mu'tazila, Qadariyya, Mufawwida, Jabariyya, Jahmiyya, Mu'attila, Mushabbiha, Mujassima, Karamiyya, Salimiyya. Notice they are all innovating sects.
This list shows al-Ash'ari's comprehensive refutations.
3
Understand Ibn Asakir's challenge
Ibn Asakir presents three conditional scenarios: if the opponent thinks refuting innovators is bid'ah, then he is foolish; if he thinks tawhid is bid'ah and anthropomorphism is Sunnah, then he is ruined; if he accuses al-Ash'ari of innovation in some issues, let him specify.
4
Reflect on the rhetorical force
Ibn Asakir uses sarcasm ('bald man') and logical dilemmas to show the opponent's position is self-contradictory. The true defender of Sunnah is not the opponent but al-Ash'ari.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله ( أن الله عز وجل لا يخلى الأرض من قائل عليم وعالم حكيم يقول الحق ويدفع الباطل ، ولا يدع لذى بدعة قولا يعلو ولا أمراً . فقد صدق ولكن ليس هو ممن وصفه بهذه الصفة إذ لم يتحقق يسمو كونه من أهل العلم ولا من ذوى المعرفة ، ولكن هم العلماء الذين بالغ في ذمهم وأغرق لفرط جهله وسوء عقده في شتمهم وأما قوله ( لا معروف أفضل من السنة ولا منكر أشد من البدعة. فانظروا بعين التحقيق إلى مقالة هذا القرعة لتعلموا أهو أشد تسننا وأقوى في العلم تمكنا أم من أشتهرت ردوده على جميع المبتدعة من أصناف الخوارج وطوائف المتشيعة وانتشرت تصانيفه فى الابطال لمذاهب المعتزلة القدرية والإنكار على من يقول بأقوال المفوضة الجبرية والاصطلام لحجج المعطلة الجهمية والمحق لتعلقات المشبهة الجسمية من الكرامية والسالمية بالحجج السمعية والبراهين العقلية فإن اعتقد أن الرد على أصحاب البدع بدعة فقد تحقق كل ذي لب تسميتي إياه قرعة وإن اعتقد أن البدعة اعتقاد التنزيه والتوحيد والسنة القول بالتشبيه والميل إلى التقليد فبئس ما اعتقد وويل له مما تقلد ، وإن كان يبدع الأشعري رحمه الله في بعض المسائل الأدلة الاقلة فليذكر ما ابتدع فيه حتى نسمع ما عنده عليه من
As for his saying: 'Allah does not leave the earth devoid of a truthful speaker and a wise scholar who speaks the truth and repels falsehood, and does not leave for any innovator a statement that rises nor an affair.' He has spoken truthfully, but he is not among those described with this attribute, for he has not attained to be of the people of knowledge nor of the possessors of understanding. Rather, they are the scholars whom he has excessively condemned and drowned due to his extreme ignorance and bad belief in reviling them. And as for his saying: 'There is no known good better than the Sunnah, and no known evil more severe than bid'ah.' Look with the eye of verification at the statement of this bald man to know whether he is more strongly adhering to Sunnah and more firmly established in knowledge, or the one whose refutations against all innovators from the various branches of Khawarij and groups of Shia are famous, and whose books have spread in invalidating the schools of the Mu'tazila Qadariyya and in denouncing those who say the sayings of the Mufawwida Jabariyya, and in seizing the arguments of the Jahmiyya Mu'attila, and in proving the attachments of the Mujassima Mushabbiha from the Karamiyya and Salimiyya with scriptural evidences and rational proofs. If he believes that refuting the people of bid'ah is itself bid'ah, then every possessor of intellect has verified my calling him 'bald.' And if he believes that bid'ah is believing in transcendence and tawhid, and that Sunnah is saying anthropomorphism and inclining to blind imitation, then evil is what he believes, and woe to him from what he imitates. And if he declares al-Ash'ari an innovator in some issues of the few evidences, let him mention what he innovated so that we may hear what he has against him.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage refutes two more claims. First, the opponent says Allah never leaves the earth without a truthful wise scholar who repels falsehood. Ibn Asakir agrees with the principle but denies that the opponent qualifies as such a scholar. In fact, the opponent has condemned the real scholars. Second, the opponent asserts that no good is better than Sunnah and no evil worse than bid'ah. Ibn Asakir challenges the opponent's consistency: the opponent claims to uphold Sunnah, but al-Ash'ari and his followers are the ones who have actually refuted all innovating sects (Khawarij, Shia, Mu'tazila, Jabariyya, Jahmiyya, Mujassima, etc.). If the opponent thinks refuting innovators is bid'ah, then he is foolish. If he thinks that believing in tawhid (transcendence) is bid'ah and anthropomorphism is Sunnah, then he is ruined. If he accuses al-Ash'ari of innovating in some issues, let him specify.

Key Terms
السنة
البدعة
المبتدعة
الخوارج
المتشيعة
المعتزلة
القدرية
المفوضة
الجبرية
المعطلة
الجهمية
المشبهة
الجسمية
الكرامية
السالمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the opponent is a defender of Sunnah because he praises it.
Correction: Ibn Asakir shows that the opponent's condemnation of scholars like al-Ash'ari, who actually refute innovations, reveals that the opponent is not a true defender of Sunnah; rather, al-Ash'ari and his followers are.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, what does al-Ash'ari and his followers actually do regarding innovation?
A) They ignore innovations
B) They write refutations against all innovating sects
C) They support innovation
D) They are themselves innovators

Key Takeaway
True Sunnah is defended not by those who attack scholars but by those who refute innovations with evidence, as al-Ash'ari did.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed someone's critique of your beliefs as bid'ah without examining the evidence? How does Ibn Asakir's challenge expose your own potential for blind partisanship, and will you commit to listening fairly next time?
?
Is there a scholar you admire that you would defend without considering whether their actions might actually contradict the Sunnah? How does this passage push you to weigh evidence over loyalty, and what will you do to change?
?
When you hear the word 'Sunnah', does it evoke a feeling of pride or a call to action? This lesson shows that true Sunnah involves active refutation of falsehood—what falsehood in your circles are you avoiding to confront, and what step will you take today?

The Salimiyya Sect and Its Anthropomorphic Beliefs
Definition of the Salimiyya sect and its anthropomorphic beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core beliefs of the Salimiyya sect and why they are classified as anthropomorphists.

Core Idea
The Salimiyya claim Allah is seen in human form — pure anthropomorphism.

The Salimiyya are an extreme sect that emerged in Basra, named after al-Hasan al-Salimi. Their beliefs about Allah and the Quran are deeply problematic. This passage from Ibn 'Asakir outlines their key doctrines and situates them within the broader category of the Mushabbiha (anthropomorphists).

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the first paragraph carefully. Note the key terms: السالمية, المشبهة, صورة آدمى.
2
Identify the three main beliefs
The passage lists three specific beliefs of the Salimiyya: seeing Allah in human form, hearing Allah in recitation, and dead experiencing physical activities. Find each one.
3
Understand the sect's origin and affiliation
Note the founder and the fact that many hadith scholars and jurists belonged to this sect, including al-Ahwazi.
This sets up the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(1) السالمية قرقة من المشبهة يقولون أن الله تعالى يرى في صورة آدمى وأنه تعالي يقرأ على لسان كل قارئ وأنهم إذا سمعوا القرآن من قارئ يرون أنهم إنما يسمعونه من الله تعالى ويعتقدون أن الميت يأكل في القبر ويشرب وينكح إلى غير ذلك ، وهذه النحلة معروفة بالبصرة وسوادها بالسالمية نسبة إلى مقالة الحسن بن محمد بن أحمد بن سالم السالمي البصري وابنه أبي عبد الله المتصوف وإلى هذه النحلة الشنيعة ينتسب كثيرون من أهل الحديث والمتفقهة والأهوازى هذا من جملة هولاء
( ۲ ) يريد بهما ما أخرجه الأهوازى فى كتابه المذكور ) أن الله تعالى لما أراد أن يخلق نفسه خلق الخيل فأجراها حتى عرقت ثم خلق نفسه من ذلك العرق ) و ( رأيت ربي يوم عرفة بعرفات على جمل أحمر عليه إزاران وهو يقول قد سمحت قد غفرت الا المظالم ) وهما مما لا يرويه عاقل ولا مسلم وكم له فيه من الفاضحات . قال الحاكم أنبأنا إسماعيل بن محمد الشعراني أخبرت عن محمد بن شجاع الثلجي أخبرني حبان بن هلال عن حماد بن سلمه عن أبى المهزم عن أبي هريرة .. ( ... خلق خيلا فأجراها فعرقت الخلق نفسه من ذلك العرق ( أهـ . وهو موضوع أتهم بعضهم بوضعه ابن شجاع ولا مخل لاتهام مثله بقول إسماعيل ( أخبرت عنه ، فمن ذا الذي أخبره عنه أسمع منه سماعا أو أخبر هو كذلك وما مبلغ ثقة هذا وذاك فليتق الله الخصوم أن ينسبوا هذه القرية إلى فقي، مثله في علمه ودينه ووجاهته وخاتمته وأن هو كان شجى في حلوق المشبهة )
(1) The Salimiyya is a sect of the anthropomorphists. They say that Allah is seen in the form of a human, and that He recites on the tongue of every reciter, and that when they hear the Quran from a reciter, they think they are hearing it from Allah. They also believe that the dead eat, drink, and have intercourse in the grave, etc. This school of thought is known in Basra and its environs as the Salimiyya, attributed to the doctrine of al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Salim al-Salimi al-Basri and his son Abu Abd Allah al-Mutasawwif. Many of the people of hadith and the fuqaha belong to this ugly school, and al-Ahwazi is one of them.
(2) By them he refers to what al-Ahwazi narrated in his aforementioned book: 'That Allah, when He wanted to create His self, created horses and made them run until they sweated, then He created His self from that sweat,' and 'I saw my Lord on the Day of Arafah at Arafat on a red camel, wearing two garments, saying: "I have forgiven, I have forgiven, except for injustices."' These are things that no sane person or Muslim would narrate. How many disgraceful things does he have in it! Al-Hakim said: Isma'il ibn Muhammad al-Sha'rani informed us: it was narrated to me from Muhammad ibn Shuja' al-Thalji: Hiban ibn Hilal narrated to me from Hammad ibn Salama from Abu al-Muhazzam from Abu Hurayra... '...He created horses and made them run so they sweated, then He created His self from that sweat.' End of quote. It is fabricated; some accused Ibn Shuja' of fabricating it. There is no room to accuse the likes of him (Ibn Shuja'?) with the statement of Isma'il 'I was informed about him.' So who is it that informed him about him? Did he hear from him directly or was he informed likewise? And what is the level of trustworthiness of this one and that? So let the opponents fear Allah that they attribute this village (?) to a faqih like him in his knowledge, religion, prestige, and end, and that it was a thorn in the throats of the anthropomorphists.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage consists of two explanatory notes (footnotes) that the author added. The first defines the Salimiyya sect, a subgroup of the anthropomorphists (المشبهة). They believe Allah is seen in human form, that He recites on the tongue of every Quran reciter, and that the dead experience physical activities in the grave. This sect is named after al-Hasan al-Salimi and his son, and many hadith scholars and jurists belong to it, including al-Ahwazi. The second note exposes two fabricated hadiths from al-Ahwazi's book: the creation of God's self from horse sweat, and seeing God riding a camel at Arafah. The author declares these narrations to be unacceptable by any sane or Muslim. He then provides a chain for one of them and notes that it is fabricated (موضوع), with some accusing Muhammad ibn Shuja' of fabricating it. He questions the reliability of the transmission and warns opponents not to attribute such absurdities to a respected faqih (likely al-Ash'ari or someone else).

Key Terms
السالمية
المشبهة
صورة آدمى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Salimiyya are considered a mainstream Sunni sect.
Correction: Ibn 'Asakir labels them as anthropomorphists (المشبهة) and their beliefs are deviant.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do the Salimiyya believe about hearing the Quran?
A) They believe the Quran is created.
B) They think they hear Allah when hearing a reciter.
C) They believe the Quran is eternal.
D) They deny hearing anything from Allah.

Key Takeaway
The Salimiyya sect holds anthropomorphic beliefs about Allah's form and speech, and was widespread in Basra.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you ever imagine Allah's voice coming through your tongue? How does the Salimiyya's extreme view challenge you to uphold Allah's transcendence while still believing the Quran is His speech?
?
The Salimiyya believed the dead experience physical pleasures like eating and drinking in the grave. How does your belief about the nature of barzakh life affect the way you prepare for death today?
?
This sect explicitly pictures Allah in human form. Are there any subtle mental images you hold of Allah that might border on anthropomorphism? What concrete steps will you take to purify your belief about Allah's attributes?

Exposing Fabricated Hadiths: The Horse Sweat and Camel Ride Narrations
Exposure of two fabricated hadiths and criticism of their chain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the content and status of two fabricated hadiths about Allah's creation and appearance, and the importance of refuting such forgeries.

Core Idea
Fabricated hadiths about Allah's self and form are dangerous lies.

In this passage, Ibn 'Asakir presents two shocking narrations from al-Ahwazi's book: that Allah created His self from horse sweat, and that He appeared on a camel at Arafah. These are clearly fabricated, and the author questions their transmission chain and integrity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Carefully read the second paragraph. Note the two fabricated hadiths and the chain criticism.
2
Identify the two narrations
The passage presents two narrations: (1) Allah created horses, they sweated, and He created His self from that sweat; (2) Seeing Allah on a red camel at Arafah. Understand why these are absurd.
3
Examine the chain and authenticity
The author provides a chain for the first narration and notes it is fabricated (موضوع). He questions the reliability of the transmitters and warns opponents not to attribute such lies to a respected scholar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author warns against defending a respected scholar despite clear evidence of forgery. Are you willing to admit when a teacher, scholar, or group you follow is wrong, even if it is uncomfortable? How does your attachment to personalities hinder your pursuit of truth?
?
These fabricated hadiths were used to support a distorted view of Allah. Are there popular teachings or anecdotes you cherish that might have weak foundations? Will you examine them honestly, even if it means letting go of something you once held dear?
